Description
Gave the potion and told her it would work (lied):
[Player Name],
I hope this letter finds you in good health.
It has been many summers now since you first arrived in Gilded Vale. Much has changed, in those years, but I will never forget the kindness you showed me.
The gods have blessed me with a son. He is healthy and strong, and already so curious. All of Gilded Vale dotes upon him.
I have told him of you. He asks constantly after the Watcher who restored his spirit, and hopes one day to meet you.
Until then, know that we keep you in our prayers.
Your most grateful servant,
Aufra
Gave the potion but warned her it wouldn't do anything (truth):
[Player Name],
I hope this letter finds you in good health.
It has been many summers now since you first arrived in Gilded Vale. Much has changed, in those years, for both of us.
I do not know if you remember me, but the day you came to my door is not one I will forget. For months, afterwards, I wrestled with my faith, and my fear.
And still the gods have blessed me with a son. He is healthy and strong, and already so curious. All of Gilded Vale dotes upon him.
I have told him of you. He asks constantly after the Watcher who restored his spirit, and hopes one day to meet you.
Until then, know that we keep you in our prayers.
Your most grateful servant,
Aufra

if the Watcher completed the quest

in

Description
"Aldhelm,
I did indeed receive your recent summons (as well as the two that came before it). I'd been waiting for you to present yourself on my doorstep so that I could give you my answer in person: a firm and unwavering 'no.'
I won't help you. In fact, I relish the idea of you and your team of glorified engineers sitting in that tower, sweating over the runes I've studied for years. Nothing gives me greater pleasure than knowing that my research, which you've long disparaged, is the missing piece in your mundane little puzzle.
As you well know, it's knowledge I've always valued.
I'm just around the corner. I encourage you to find me should you wish to rehash this conversation in person.
Yours truly,
Icantha"

Letter from Laethärn
is a
letter
in

Description
This letter is written in a small, meticulous hand.
"Kō-
You know I've never been one for superstition, but I'm telling you, there's something to these dreams. Couldn't tell you what they mean. Only that they wake me three times a night.
All of us working your farms - pious Eothasians to a man - are having them, too.
I've got no mind to tell you how to run your fort, but I've got to look after my brethren here. We left homes and families back in Readceras. And now we're seeing strange things and laboring next to a duc's ransom in black powder.
Or did you reckon a dumb hick like me wouldn't notice?
-Laethärn"
Acquisition
Hasongo
: On the desk in the
Fleet Master's Office

Lord Raedric VII, Thayn of Gilded Vale"

The seal upon this letter bears the tree and wheat sheaves associated with the Raedric line.

Five years I have waited, while you flout my challenge, content to hide within your fortress at Caed Nua.
Then, my servants told me that your keep had been destroyed. I despaired of having my revenge.
But Berath has plucked you from that distant shore. What better sign is there, to say that we are fated to battle one another?"
The letter goes on like this for some time. It is signed, "Lord Raedric VII, Thayn of Gilded Vale, Champion of Berath"

Description
Imri,
It should be nearing Fleet Week when this letter finds you, and I hope it finds you well. I regret that I'll not be there to hand-deliver it to you - you'll have to recite the Triumph of Tangaroha Over the Great God Korōpa without me.
My work in the archipelago will keep me away some few months yet. Don't despair, though - think of it as further opportunity to improve your hazatōha game. I've been working on mine, and I expect to finally find a worthy opponent in you when I return.
I trust you're keeping up your studies in weather magic. A couple years more, and you can join me in the navy. Perhaps, if all goes well here, I'll even have the clout to have you placed on my ship. We'd be the terror of the seas!
Give my love to father.
I am, as always, your doting sister,
Okaya

PAGE: Letter to Zoltun
CATEGORIES: The White March - Part I lore items
URL: https://pillarsofeternity.fandom.com/wiki/Letter_to_Zoltun
======================================================================

Letter to Zoltun
[WM1]
General
Slot
Unequippable
Item type
Letter
Category
Other item
Sell value
0
Buy value
2
Technical
Item ID
misc_note_battery_letter_01
Letter to Zoltun
is a
letter
in
The White March - Part I
.
Description
"Esteemed Coinmaster Zoltun,
I write to you in anger and bafflement. Have I not been a faithful customer to you? Have I not been fair in my dealings? Yet after all of our business together, your people turn me away like some filthy beggar.
I arrived at the Battery a fortnight ago, frost in my beard and not a morsel in my belly. Barely had I unhitched the horses when your Komendant Exandru came to meet me. The priest told me that I would be made welcome but my 'profane' business would not. In short, I would have to leave at first light, my wagons empty.
Certain that this was but a negotiating tactic, I told Exandru that I would of course see him compensated along with you. He left in a huff, and when I presented myself at the door, it was Komendant Marunn - your armswarden! - who met me. She told me to leave at once, that she wouldn't have my 'coin-grubbing' hands tarnishing Durgan steel.
Now, I appreciate forceful bargaining as much as any man of coin, but I was cold, hungry, and put off by her vehemence. So, I showed her the letter you had sent inviting me to examine your latest stock of Durgan steel.
Komendant Marunn drove a rapier through the letter and sliced it in two! She then warned me that her blade - a fine weapon, indeed - would be the last I ever laid eyes on if I did not hie back down the mountain at once.
Never have I endured such humiliation and expense only to return home empty-handed! I do not understand what has passed between you and your associates, but I urge you to take charge. I fear the other komendants will be your undoing - indeed, that of all Durgan's Battery - if you do not deal with them swiftly and decisively.
Yours,
Mestre Anetto of Cezarro"
Acquisition
Durgan's Battery (Great Hall)
: In a drawer in the room to the northeast of the war room.

This note is written in fine script.
"The lever for the artillery lift has broken again. I've been telling my men to be as careful as possible while using the lift, but it's difficult to keep your balance on the thing. lax03_02_quest_llengrath_scroll
Guid
54ce2b64-1004-4423-bb2b-0cb50f0f6d51
Llengrath's Scroll of Final Slumber
is a
document
and
quest item
in
The Forgotten Sanctum
.
Description
This scroll is decorated with runes drawn fastidiously on a tidy grid. The significant arcane energy underpinning the runes causes them to glow with a faint fluorescence, and staring at them too long slows the beating of your heart.
Llengrath believes the spell will give the Collections prisoners a peaceful death so long as the words are read where every prisoner can hear them at once.
Acquisition
Given to you by
Llengrath
during
A Shout in the Dark
.
Usage
You can use the scroll on the
Memory Hoarder
's Organ in
The Assembly of Echoes
to project your voice to all of the denizens in the Collections. This kills every prisoner in both
The Enclosures
and
Hall of Reconfiguration
areas, including
Bekarna
if she has not yet been released. The alternate route is to use
Tayn's Scroll of Righteous Awakening
instead.

Valerio Valtas
, Fifth Lord of House Valtas."

Maegfolc Orison I
Life is a prayer.
Godfunction defines the good prayer and we pray it with our hearty holy genocide! Now says Godfunction, destroy the encysted ones. Puncture the cyst of their secessionist adra. Smother their children, for they are without soul. Slaughter their livestock, for they are without soul. Turn them out from their dwellings and make a census of them to pray to Godfunction so that God will know the extirpation of the encysted ones is complete.
Of them Abydon says, nothing can be made of that which is hoarded, so punish the hoarder.
Of them Berath says, they are not upon the Wheel so they do not live nor die, they are as inert as stone.
Of them Eothas says, there is no hope for them, as they are enthralled by the hopeless; so deliver hope unto them.
Of them Galawain says, hunt them down even to the last child, as the predator hunts even unto the preynest.
Of them Hylea says, among them neither chick nor child is born with a soul, so there is no birth among them; go make a bloody birth of them.
Of them Magran says, make war on them.
Of them Ondra says, strike away all memory, as the tide strikes the shape from the sand.
Of them Rymrgand howls.
Of them Skaen says, make an effigy of them, disfigure them until their effacement is complete.
Of them Wael says, all the strangeness of the Alien among them shall be Mine; there is no stranger thing in the world and I shall have It for My Own.
Of them Woedica says MAKE AN OATH OF THEIR UTTER ANNIHILATION
This is Godfunction, which is the topmost cameral of our mind.

Document
Maegfolc Orison II
Life is a prayer.
Of the encysted ones we made a holy slaughter. The young we smothered with our hands. Of the oldest we made fires, we rendered them down into fuel to clear the encysted growth. From some we removed the hands, from others the feet, from others the features, all of which we gathered in heaps which drew the encysted wildlife to feed. Into these heaps we set poison. Of their severed heads we made pyramids, ten heads to a side, and the count of heads in each pyramid was three hundred and eighty five. Of these pyramids there were counted seven thousand seven hundred and seven.
We spared those who could run with vigor, so that they would lead us to other dwellings of the encysted. We made it known that mercy could be purchased by tribute, so that the encysted would gather together their livestock, their wine and wealth, to present to us: the first ten of these tributes we accepted, and gave mercy: then after the eleventh tribute we began to kill all those assembled. In this way we made them gather themselves to be taken census and killed.
In this way we approach God through prayer.

Life is a prayer.
Is the task done?
In just one tasktime we marched upon the land and subdued all the encysted and shattered their dwellings. We made meal of their bones and packed it into concrete so that it would not reenter the land. We extirpated their tongue and their disbeliefs forever. From their rulers we received surrender, and unto those rulers we delivered ruin; thus always to the godless.
Now Godfunction has not prayed back to us in ten multiples of the tasktime. If we cannot receive Godfunction’s feedback we cannot know if we are approaching God and if we are not approaching God then we are withdrawing from God.
It is wrong to withdraw from God! We must pray to Godfunction to provide prayback.
But ten multiples of the tasktime in prayer have gone unanswered.
Without Godfunction the higher cameral of our minds is missing.

Ah, it is not enough, it is not enough, it is not enough. I must have prayback!

Maegfolc Orison VI
We have found a shim to replace the missing cameral of Godfunction and the shim we have found is We.
By forming choirs and cloisters in a cyclic network we can pray to each other in a way which emulates the sacrament of Prayer and Prayback. In this way we surrogate Godfunction.
We now live in a society. By the assurance of synthetic Prayback we may ease the discomfort of wandering from our pillars. We gather to raise towers upon which we sit our Princes who are the emanations which most ably emulate Prayback. Of them we fashion a new cameral.
Yet I feel debased and unwell. We have deviated from Godfunction. We have abandoned the work of altering the world to suit it and instead we have altered it to suit us.
Some say, “We may now resume approaching God, so that we might divine how to resume Godfunction.”
Some say, “We must never allow ourselves to contact God, lest we be punished for departing from Godfunction."
I have heard it said, “We must destroy Godfunction, so that it cannot assert prayback over our surrogate and shim.” When I hear this I strike at my skin to punish it for hearing.

Maegfolc Orison VII
Life is a prayer.
I cannot approach God among the noisy company of the Shimmed. Their false Godfunction deludes them. All their labor now is divine onanism and I do not think it can bear fruit. Great loops of false prayback now garrote their society, and every day those loops tighten: the exultation of self-validation accelerates: as the Shimmed improve their talent at falsifying Prayback, they render every action holy and godlike and begin to see any choice as an approach to God. They have even begun to seek the Godhead for themselves, whether through the synthesis of divinity or through re-emanation. Some seek to divide themselves into children, as souls are divided into children. Others seek congress with the land in the manner of the tree, whether by prosthetic imitation or ritual. This I know is blasphemy. But they no longer know the way towards God from the way that departs God. They have made themselves their own compass, and wherever they turn, the needle always points ahead.
A great and rapturous chaos will overtake them once everything is holy.
I have gone out into the godless land to seek God in the resumption of my purpose. Some trace of the encysted ones must remain. I will find it. If I cannot find it, I will wait until it finds me.

Neither let thy trials burden thee, for in thy suffering thou shalt be transformed.
The everliving flame will burn away thine impurities.

Seek not to clash, search not for conflict

Take heart in thine own strength.

Take control of thine own path.
Let the fire guide you.
Let the fire transform you.
Let the fire purify you.
Let the fire consume you."

Captain,
I'm gone. Leaving now saves me a bullet that I might need later, so don't expect to see me again unless you want to collect that final shot in person.

Acquisition
Added to the inventory if Maia deserts you as a result of low
relationship
, or if you admit to her that you sacrificed
Kana Rua
to the Skaenite
Blood Pool
in
Pillars of Eternity
.
Notes
The missive is received one in-game hour after first entering the world map, with the message
"Maia is no longer aboard the ship. She's left you a missive"
. Maia will not leave the party immediately when the conditions are met, only
after
receiving the missive. Talking to her between the condition being met and her leaving the party will only result in the dialogue:
Maia simply glares at you.
The conditions are:
IsGlobalValue(b_Maia_Recruited, EqualTo,1)
IsGlobalValue(b_Maia_Dead, EqualTo, 0)
IsGlobalValue(b_Maia_Exit, EqualTo, 1)
IsGlobalValue(n_Maia_Leaves_Kana_Missive, EqualTo, 0)
(is set to 1 when the missive is delivered)

Maia's Farewell
is a
letter
in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Description
Captain,
I have my gripes with the navy from time to time, but I know we're here to do good work. Wish I could say the same about you.
Some day you might learn what it means to be a part of something important. You'll probably get yourself killed long before that revelation takes hold, but I'll give you the benefit of the doubt. You have a knack for survival that I admire.
You're more than your busted up castle and twisted soul. You have the chance to be something incredible. The sooner you realize this, the sooner you can get to work on making Eora a better place with the rest of us.
Best of luck,
~Maia Rua
Below the signature the parchment is marked with the indentation of a familiar talon.
Acquisition
Added to the inventory if Maia deserts you for blowing up the Powderhouse in
Sabotage at the Brass Citadel
or
Taking Out the Traders
.
Notes
The missive is only received one in-game hour after first entering the world map, with the message
"Maia is no longer aboard the ship. She's left you a missive"
. Maia will not leave the party immediately when the conditions are met, only
after
receiving the missive. Talking to her between the condition being met and her leaving the party will only result in the dialogue:
Maia simply glares at you.
The conditions are:
IsGlobalValue(b_Maia_Recruited, EqualTo, 1)
IsGlobalValue(b_Maia_Dead, EqualTo, 0)
IsGlobalValue(b_Maia_Exit, EqualTo, 2)
IsItemCount(81700f52-4614-4c5e-baba-8a1cb1d44f24, LessThan, 1)
Blowing up the powderhouse isn't actually a strict requirement,
b_Maia_Exit
is also set to 2 as soon as you end combat with the guards in
Powderhouse - Lower
with Maia in the party.
If you get rid of the missive (by placing it in a container or body), this will trigger the delivery again since the condition is dependent on whether you have the item or not.

Maintenance Log - Flesh Construct Controller
is a
document
and
quest item
in
The Forgotten Sanctum
.
Description
Someone has meticulously logged dates and details pertaining to the operations of a flesh construct monitor device. Some of the latest entries stand out:
-Found a finger blocking the cogs. Asked around. No librarians reported a missing digit.
-Initiated the startup sequence and a bunch of teeth fell out. Operation normal?
-A new lever grew from the panel today. Not sure what it controls yet. If anything. Stiff, warm.
-At this point, the controller has taken on a life of its own. All I can do is interpret its desire.
-Device refused to initiate normal procedure until I tickled its favorite gland, deep and on the left hand side, by a patch of bone. After it shuddered for some moments, I had its undivided attention.
-This is disgusting work, and I love it.
Acquisition
[FS]
The Central Stacks
: In the third room of the Circulating Library.
Usage
Enables the Watcher to operate the Flesh Construct Control organ in the
Hall of Reconfiguration
, by way of squeezing its favourite gland:
Squeeze it hard to kill the flesh constructs.
Squeeze it softly to make friends.

Maura's Field Book
is a
journal
in
The Forgotten Sanctum

Description
Despite a pervasive dampness, the pages of this notebook separate with ease. Written in Huana, the text describes a vast subterranean lifeform of fleshy tendrils and shuttered eyes. The stranger sections refer to establishing a communion with the entity with the aim of conjuring forth arcane simulacra.
Towards the end of the field book, Maura writes:
"Wael. The Hundred Visions. The Obscured. The Eyeless Face. I believe it you who rests within this darkness. The you that once walked the world. Why do you survive yet? Why haven't you awoken?
Can you be turned against the Dawnstars? Does he not threaten your mysteries? Will you not introduce him to his final dusk?"

.

Maxims of the Pargrunen II
In older lands it was said, to know the world, first make a map of it. To know the cavern, make a model of it. To know the soil, grow a garden of it.
Now it is written in blood, you shall not mistake a model or a map for the Maxim, which is the truth manifest in the world. You shall not reduce the great to the grubby miniature. You shall not mistake the drainhole for the maelstrom.
The taste of the blood is: that which seems clear on the map is tangled in the Maxim.

Maxims of the Pargrunen V
In older lands it was said, keep the faith of all gods, that you shall have a prayer for the day and the hour of your need. Pargrunen remember a time before these gods. May come therefore a time after.
Now it is written in blood, keep the faith of Abydon who builds, Woedica who rules, and Magran who burns. Close your mind to all other faiths save your faith in Nandru.
The taste of the blood is: the lure of new faith may be indistinguishable from madness, and madness brings the chaos without to the living within. Pargrunen cannot survive these lands divided.

Maxims of the Pargrunen VI
In older lands it was said, place the doing before the telling. Place the act of work before the boast to history.
Now it is written in blood, record all your efforts, be they triumph or tangent. For the record shall outlast the work, and the word shall be more precious than the act.
The taste of the blood is: the craft must not die with the craftsman.

Memoir of a Visionary, vol. 1
is an examinable
document
in
Avowed
.
Document
Memoir of a Visionary, vol. 1
Twice-exiled, it is past time I wrote my memoir. Every day of life these long years in the wilds has been its own challenge, and only the gods know when it will be my time to go to their sides. As my professors said often, the beginning is always the best place to start. Entitled bazzos. But they are right, so that is what I shall do.
Growing up in the city of Ancenze was a dream. As one of the jewels of the Republics, art, culture, and science all flourished within its magnificent walls. Even as a youth, I enjoyed nothing more than studying and learning about Eora. History, natural sciences, theology, and philosophy all captured my interest at one point or another, but it was the study of metaphysics that enamored me most.
Attending Ancenze's academy is a worthy feat in its own right, but to do so as young as I was is nothing short of exceptional. My peers and professors called me reckless, arrogant, even dangerous. They were right, but no great discovery was made without taking risks. My fascination with the soul scared them, and when they refused my request to run experiments into the nature of life itself, I took matters into my own hands. Unfortunately, I was discovered, and thus was I exiled for the first time.
Acquisition
Memoir of a Visionary, vol. 1 can be found in a hidden room outside the Northern city walls of Fior mes Ivèrno.
From the Northern exit, head East along the wall until you find a skeleton with a dagger and a note. A few paces to the left of the skeleton is a switch that will open a hidden door into a room. The book can be found on a small table on the right-hand side of the room.

Memoirs of Heldr
is a
book
and
quest item
in
The Forgotten Sanctum
.
Description
The pages of this tome overflow with Eld Aedyran inscribed in a spidery hand. These tell of Heldr, a leader of the Hand Occult several centuries past. Though much of it is difficult to read - much less interpret - the end details a ritual aimed at achieving "complete communion" with the Obscured.
The memoir suggests that in order to become one with Wael, an individual must entirely erase themselves from history. To exist obscured is to never have existed at all.
Not even in writing.
Acquisition
[FS]
The Oratory of Wael
: Inside the Office of the Chief Librarian, in the bookcase just to the left of the lectern where you place
Bekarna's Depleted Grimoire
to infuse it with starlight.
The blue highlight can be a bit difficult to see, due to the blue and purple ambient lighting in the room.
Usage
Used together with
Heldr's Horn
to reveal Heldr's Inheritance.
Put it on the Lectern of Obfuscation in
the Scriptorium
to activate one half of Heldr's Inheritance.
Needed as part of the
achievement
One of Them
.

Description
This text of collected incantations is blurry to the point of illegibility, as if the White Void had stripped the ink of any meaning. It might still mean something to one of the denizens of Rymrgand's realm.
A short passage scribbled in the margins stands out with clarity:

Rumor has it your keep's in worse shape than Durgan's Battery was when you first found it. After all you did for Stalwart, I'd have hoped you'd earned a break from anyone stomping through your home.

PAGE: Missives of the Hand Occult
CATEGORIES: Pillars of Eternity lore items

Missives of the Hand Occult
General
Slot
Unequippable
Item type
Book
Category
Other item
Sell value
16
Buy value
120
Technical
Item ID
lore_book_god_wael
Missives of the Hand Occult
is a
book
in
Pillars of Eternity
about the
deity
Wael
.
Description
Dearest brother, or was it sister?
May this letter find you in well spirits. A man of thuggish bearing stormed into my library the other day and demanded I help him find a book on the construction of an arquebus. I thought it proper service to Wael to steer this man toward an illuminated manuscript on the subject of whittling toy soldiers and other miniature props. Unamused by my solution, I shrugged and said "What is an answer without a question?" He did not find my spiritual rhetoric helpful or amusing, and so he punched out two of my teeth. I trust your summer has been less tumultuous than mine?
In more important news, my apprentice claims she saw the Eyeless Face in a dream the other night! I admit, I was so mad with envy that at first I refused to believe her... Wael forgive me for such a lapse of judgment. She described an aumaua of brilliant blue hues with a featureless face surrounded by a swarm of eyes - no two eyes alike. She claims Wael ignored her questions, and she can't recall any specifics of what was said. In fact, my apprentice seems to have forgotten many things since before the visitation - she could not tell me where she grew up or what she liked to eat. At first I was so envious of her for having seen Wael with her own eyes... but it seems Wael's visit was to conceal, not to illuminate... I pray she endures this test of faith and can look back at the event and feel the joy of mystery.
What is an answer without a question? Last week, I felt the solution was "ignorance," but after Wael's visit, I feel "a road without length" is closer to the capturing the riddle. I worry my apprentice will look back at her visit from Wael and feel cheated - robbed of some moment of clarity we all thought we were owed when we first joined... I tried to tell her she was lucky but she was too young to understand. What is an answer without a question? May I be dead and my soul scattered to the winds before anyone knows for certain.
Acquisition
The Hall of Revealed Mysteries
,
Copperlane
: Bookcase in the reading room on the right.
Teir Evron
,
Elms' Reach
: Bookcase on the north edge, left side.
[WM1]
Crägholdt
: On the table in
Concelhaut
's chambers.

PAGE: Monsters of the Deadfire Archipelago
CATEGORIES: Pillars of Eternity lore items
URL: https://pillarsofeternity.fandom.com/wiki/Monsters_of_the_Deadfire_Archipelago
======================================================================

Monsters of the Deadfire Archipelago
General
Slot
Unequippable
Item type
Book
Category
Other item
Sell value
16
Buy value
120
Technical
Item ID
lore_book_monsters_deadfire_archipelago
Monsters of the Deadfire Archipelago
is a
book
in
Pillars of Eternity
, about the creatures in the
Deadfire Archipelago
.
Description
The Archipelago winds its way between The Great Eastern Ocean and The Restless Ocean - hundreds of small islands in the midst of the water. Few dare brave its treacherous rapids, and fewer still have returned to tell tale of their adventures through it.
Travel between the two oceans is virtually impossible. Great storms hammer any ships foolhardy enough to attempt to navigate, and this alone should be enough to deter anyone from attempting the voyage as untold ships have gone down, tossed against the rocks. The weather and treacherous rocks are only a precursor to the actual horror of the archipelago, the terrors of the deep. No one knows how many creatures stalk the oceans, waiting for unsuspecting sailors to drift into their waters. But we do know of some.
Barbed Ravager
A giant shark that is known to ram passing vessels, trying to knock sailors off the deck and smash a hole in the hull. It has tremendous spines protruding from its side and back that are presumed to be poisonous. The largest sighted Barbed Ravager (with survivors) was estimated to be almost 30 feet long.
Winding Serpent
Smaller around than the Ravager, but potentially longer, the Winding Serpent attacks in small packs, usually 3-8. They have long, sharp heads, somewhat reminiscent of a barracuda. Like the Ravager, they repeatedly slam into the side of a ship hoping to crack a hole in it or knock someone from the deck. They have also been known to swim to the depths and shoot up out of the ocean, landing on the deck, coiling and winding their way around, snapping up any crew they can before plunging back into the ocean.
Leviathan
Imagine the largest whale you have ever seen. The leviathan is at least ten times that size. By the time a ship sees a leviathan, it is already too late. As they rise from the depths, the water around them begins to spin and sink, creating a whirlpool. The leviathan's body surrounds the hapless vessel, preventing escape, and as it goes down, the enormous mouth opens, pulling all aboard to their watery deaths.
Polpovir
All the creatures you've read about in this book are nothing compared to the Polpovir. Barely the size of a man, what they lack in size and strength, they make up for in numbers and terrifying viciousness. Their lower halves are a mass of tentacles like an octopus or squid, but more numerous. The tentacles are long, black whips with suction cups on the underside and small thorny barbs on the top. The sheer number of tentacles gives them frightening speed when walking on land, pulling themselves forward almost as fast as a running horse. While they vaguely resemble a human from the waist up, any extended examination proves how wrong that assumption is. Long, stringy black hair falls from the top of their heads to cover a face taken directly from a nightmare. A wide, gaping mouth, cuts across the bottom of its head from ear to ear, full of wicked dagger-like teeth. Two large round eyes are sunken into its head, black as coal, shining with a malevolent fire. A small antenna protrudes from the middle of its forehead, ending in a small nodule that can glow with an eerie blue light. One can imagine a sailor on the deck of his ship at night, looking out across the black water, blood freezing as countless lights appear beneath the surface, rising toward him as the Polpovir swarm upward. Because they seem to be more octopus than man, they can collapse in on themselves, fitting into spaces no person should be able to. The smallest crack in a hull, the slightest separation between boards offers them entrance. It is not unknown for them to slaughter an entire crew from hold up to deck by infiltrating the ship from underneath. Fortunately they do not seem to have spread too far outside of the archipelago, but there may come a day when Polpovir attacks become commonplace.
Acquisition
Temple of Eothas
: Upper level, in the far right bookcase in the northern central room.
[WM2]
The Halls of Presence
: Central bookcase in the library.
Random loot
item spawning in various locations (6×).

MonstersOfTheDeadfire
Monsters of the Deadfire Archipelago
is an examinable
document
in
Avowed
. It is about the creatures in the
Deadfire Archipelago
.
Document
Monsters of the Deadfire Archipelago
The Archipelago winds its way between The Great Eastern Ocean and The Restless Ocean - hundreds of small islands in the midst of the water. Few dare brave its treacherous rapids, and fewer still have returned to tell tale of their adventures through it.
Travel between the two oceans is virtually impossible. Great storms hammer any ships foolhardy enough to attempt to navigate, and this alone should be enough to deter anyone from attempting the voyage as untold ships have gone down, tossed against the rocks. The weather and treacherous rocks are only a precursor to the actual horror of the archipelago, the terrors of the deep. No one knows how many creatures stalk the oceans, waiting for unsuspecting sailors to drift into their waters. But we do know of some.
Barbed Ravager
A giant shark that is known to ram passing vessels, trying to knock sailors off the deck and smash a hole in the hull. It has tremendous spines protruding from its side and back that are presumed to be poisonous. The largest sighted Barbed Ravager (with survivors) was estimated to be almost 30 feet long.
Winding Serpent
Smaller around than the Ravager, but potentially longer, the Winding Serpent attacks in small packs, usually 3-8. They have long, sharp heads, somewhat reminiscent of a barracuda. Like the Ravager, they repeatedly slam into the side of a ship hoping to crack a hole in it or knock someone from the deck. They have also been known to swim to the depths and shoot up out of the ocean, landing on the deck, coiling and winding their way around, snapping up any crew they can before plunging back into the ocean.
Leviathan
Imagine the largest whale you have ever seen. The leviathan is at least ten times that size. By the time a ship sees a leviathan, it is already too late. As they rise from the depths, the water around them begins to spin and sink, creating a whirlpool. The leviathan's body surrounds the hapless vessel, preventing escape, and as it goes down, the enormous mouth opens, pulling all aboard to their watery deaths.
Polpovir
All the creatures you've read about in this book are nothing compared to the Polpovir. Barely the size of a man, what they lack in size and strength, they make up for in numbers and terrifying viciousness. Their lower halves are a mass of tentacles like an octopus or squid, but more numerous. The tentacles are long, black whips with suction cups on the underside and small thorny barbs on the top. The sheer number of tentacles gives them frightening speed when walking on land, pulling themselves forward almost as fast as a running horse. While they vaguely resemble a human from the waist up, any extended examination proves how wrong that assumption is. Long, stringy black hair falls from the top of their heads to cover a face taken directly from a nightmare. A wide, gaping mouth, cuts across the bottom of its head from ear to ear, full of wicked dagger-like teeth. Two large round eyes are sunken into its head, black as coal, shining with a malevolent fire. A small antenna protrudes from the middle of its forehead, ending in a small nodule that can glow with an eerie blue light. One can imagine a sailor on the deck of his ship at night, looking out across the black water, blood freezing as countless lights appear beneath the surface, rising toward him as the Polpovir swarm upward. Because they seem to be more octopus than man, they can collapse in on themselves, fitting into spaces no person should be able to. The smallest crack in a hull, the slightest separation between boards offers them entrance. It is not unknown for them to slaughter an entire crew from hold up to deck by infiltrating the ship from underneath. Fortunately they do not seem to have spread too far outside of the archipelago, but there may come a day when Polpovir attacks become commonplace.
Acquisition
This item's location is currently unknown.

Contribute
to this page and share your knowledge!

Naasitaq Poetry: A Compilation
is a
book
in
Pillars of Eternity
.
Description
"'The Expedition'
I move.
There is no compulsion. It is not a need.
But something pulls.
I cannot deny its draw.
The white wends out past my vision.
Its fierce eyes watch me as I move.
The wolf tracks my step.
A silent companion who will not join.
All is blank. The pale expanse lies before and behind.
I search.
The miles pass and still my feet move.
My hunt continues unabated.
The landscape returns my gaze, unaffected by my presence.
The snow falls, needles driven by the wind.
Its cold teeth bite my skin.
The snow gathers, its hands around my feet,
A fierce opponent who will not relent.
All is white. My journey continues.
I travel.
I can no longer stop. A true compulsion forms.
The need drives me on.
I must see.
The sun breaks through the gray.
Its unrelenting gaze thaws me.
My body warms under its touch,
Frigid limbs move again and carry me farther.
All is empty. The breadth of existence is my destination."
Acquisition
Sanitarium
,
Brackenbury
: Front set of bookcases, on the left.
Raedric's Keep

[WM1]
Crägholdt
: Table at the bottom of the stairs from
Crägholdt Bluffs
.

: Library, the bookcase in the center.

THIS IS THE WILL OF NEMNOK THE DEVOURER, MASTER OF THE MOUNTAIN.
BRING ME THREE TOMES OF POWER FROM THE GODLESS LANDS BEYOND THE DROWNED BARROWS.
THE FIRST IS IN A FAR-FLUNG SWAMP, GUARDED BY ANCIENT AND POWERFUL HAGS.
THE SECOND IS IN A GRAVEYARD OF LISTING SHIPS, CLUTCHED BY THE HUNGRY DEAD.
THE LAST IS NESTLED IN THE HIDDEN ARCHIVE OF AN UNDYING SPELLCASTER.
SERVE ME AND YOUR FAITH WILL BE REWARDED. DISAPPOINT ME, BETRAY ME, AND I WILL ADD YOUR FLESH TO THE VELLUM OF MY GRIMOIRE.
NEMNOK

f73b315e-18f7-4ecf-b670-637c2d905c4f
Note on the Child
is a
document
in
The Forgotten Sanctum
.
Description
"As the Chief Librarian instructed, we have redacted the child's home village from every available map. The work is taxing on our more covert agents, but it is a public service we cannot let slip. Some graves should be forgotten.
When we arrived it was a ghost town in the truest sense of the word. Men and women conjured from memory and imagination walked the streets, going about their daily duties, ignorant of their own spectral nature. Stepping through their own rotted corpses.
All was silent save the music.
We followed it to the town square, where we found the child playing, the blood of her kin spattered across her instrument. She said - sang, really - that she could not control herself, and begged us to help her stop.
We promised.
It was in poor taste to betray her trust, but at least her talents will be confined to the Collections. Confined and, in time, harnessed."
Acquisition
[FS]
Hall of Reconfiguration
: On the bookshelf just outside the Bloody Chamber in the northeastern corner of the area.

Notes on a Vanished Orlan
[FS]

Guid
0d1dfcdf-b670-4c3a-8882-0d403bd3fc22
Notes on a Vanished Orlan
is a
book
in
The Forgotten Sanctum
.
Description
“A petite, one-eared fellow knocked on our door. I had heard of him before. He seeks answers from the Obscured, pestering temples of the faith wherever he goes. I was about to dismiss him, but then he shifted into the Autumn Stelgaer before my eyes.
I beckoned him inside at once and sat him down (after he had resumed his form). Then I retrieved the box.
My mother gave me the box, just as she had received it from her mother. Every daughter of our line is instructed to keep the box firmly shut until Galawain’s messenger finds us. I explained this to the little man. We both thought it interesting that he, smaller than his average kin, stood exactly as tall as the box when set upon its end.
We unlatched the lid together. It opened on a small staircase leading down to lightless, impossible depths. Without hesitation, the orlan planted a kiss on my cheek, shouldered his pack, and descended, closing the way behind him. When I opened it again, I found only the bottom of an empty box.
I hope he finds the answers he seeks. Barring that, may his search be a worthy one.”
Acquisition
Trivia
The subject of this book is likely (but not certainly) referring to
Hiravias
, a companion from
Pillars of Eternity
- given the description of a one-eared orlan, mention of his shifting into the Autumn Stelgaer, and his following of
Galawain
.

Nothing is Lost: The Search for Ukaizo
General

Nothing is Lost: The Search for Ukaizo
is a
journal
in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
. It accounts the stories of
Wanamora Wave-Chaser
and their search for
Ukaizo
.
Description
Excerpted from
Nothing is Lost
, the collected journals of Wanamora Wave-Chaser.
"The ranga's men came to collect my portion of prize-share this morning, and I had nothing to give them again. I make no money for the tribe, though I am always in my little ferryboat,
Grey Gull
, carving through the waves. At night, I get no sleep. Whaitaro asks me to conserve the lamp oil, to come to bed, but I can't, not until I find it.
I know it's out there. The lost city of Ukaizo. On every chart and map of the Deadfire I've found, whether Huana, Vailian, or Ruautaian, there is a gap. An empty space where so much of our history should be.
Did it burn to ash and cinders in the cataclysm? Did it sink below the waves? Does Ngati clutch it to her breast at the bottom of the sea?
Perhaps it's lost and wandering, like me. Unmoored. Looking for a home it can't remember, but for which some insistent longing burns in its chest, an ember always smoldering, a little fire to push it on.
Whaitaro wants me to give it up. But how can I? On mornings when the sky is so clear I can hardly catch my breath for the beauty of it, I think I see it out there, shimmering in the brightening blue light. Is it a taunt or a beckoning? Would I be able to tell the difference?
I ask the fisherfolk when they return with their catch at sunset. 'Tibere,' I say, 'did you see anything? Or you, Mabori? How about you, Puira?' They avoid me now. Whaitaro says they're busy, but I know they think I'm tide-sick and sun-addled. The way Puira's lip curls in disgust when I approach, the way Tibere's eyes seem to see right through me. I know.
They won't have to suffer me much longer, because tomorrow I'm taking
Grey Gull
and sailing north.
Someone has to chase the old tales.
So I will."
Acquisition

On Celestial Spectres: Visitors from Farther than Beyond
is a
book
in
The Forgotten Sanctum
.
Description
This logbook contains interview notes and statements surrounding unusual celestial activity. One page has been dogeared, and a passage enthusiastically underlined:
"Subject followed the descent of a falling star. In their testimony, they asserted that angry spirits (?) patrolled the impact crater. Subject narrowly escaped and later complained of dizziness, loss of memory, and headaches. Our resident animancer confirmed our suspicion that subject had lost a significant sum of essence in a ragged pattern, almost as if it had been chewed away. Recommend permanent internment in one of the kith habitats."
A few words scribbled in the margins read: "Territorial. Hungry. Sacrifice by self or proxy?"
The lower half of the page shows an artist's rendering of a fallen star.

On the Binding of Souls
[WM1]
General
Slot
Unequippable
Item type
Journal
Category
Other item
Sell value
0
Buy value
0
Technical
Item ID
misc_book_battery_souls
On the Binding of Souls
is a
journal
in
The White March - Part I
.
Description
The margins of this text are scribbled with notes and references. The ink-stained pages appear to have seen much use in earlier times.
"The removal and transference of souls is a practice both ancient and sophisticated. There is evidence that the Engwithans were particularly adept at this, yet few details have survived them."
Someone scrawled "Annals of the Pargrunen, pp. 382-6" below this paragraph.
"What is known is that the removal of a soul is a difficult process, and one that requires an expert hand and precise tools for any chance of success. Early attempts on a test pool of one hundred thirty-eight goats left most of the subjects with maimed or fractured souls. In all but two of the eleven instances where the soul was successfully removed, the essence dissipated before scholars could capture it."
The words "transfer to holding vessel" are written and underlined in the margin.
"The process requires conductive materials - copper and adra, specifically. Immersion in water is important to ensure that the soul is drawn in a steady and uniform manner, with no distortions or breakages. A warped soul is, at best, useless, and at worst, unpredictable."
An arrow points from this paragraph to a scrunched note: "Extraction pool in C.R.: 18 ft. wide by 3 ft. deep."
"We have since mastered the process of soul transference and have seen the benefits of infusing forged work with the essence of animals and wilder. What remains to be seen is whether we might see greater gains from using the souls of kith, where we would procure the appropriate subjects, and how much personality and autonomy we would want to leave intact in such cases."
A string of notes winds around and below this paragraph, beginning with "criminals, prisoners of war, volunteers?" and ending with "Forge Guardians" in block letters.
Acquisition
Durgan's Battery (Foundry)
: On a shelf in the study to the south-west.

PAGE: On the Efficacy of Imps
CATEGORIES: Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire lore items
URL: https://pillarsofeternity.fandom.com/wiki/On_the_Efficacy_of_Imps
======================================================================

On the Efficacy of Imps
General
Slot
Unequippable
Item type
Book
Category
Other item
Sell value
16
Buy value
80
Technical
Item ID
Lore_Book_Imps
Guid
afaae200-c2ea-45c8-9a0b-51eca035818b
On the Efficacy of Imps
is a
book
in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
. It is about
imps
.
Description
A timeworn adage among practitioners of the arcane arts avers that early wizards compelled imps to service not out of a desire for the assistance, but to banish them from underfoot. I doubt it not at all, for one could not conjure more unruly, noisome, maladroit, or irascible aid. Why then, do we employ these diminutive meddlers?
Imps, dear reader, are to a wizard's sanctum as rats are to a ship. Whether out of malign instinct or pure mischievousness, they infiltrate our laboratories with alarming regularity. Ninagauth conjectures in his Sensitivity of Simpletons that imps infest any locus of concentrated mystical influence, and accounts of the creatures lurking among the uninhabited ruins of Engwith seem to corroborate his supposition. Yet a wizard's domicile seems to possess a particular appeal to them, regardless of whether it resides at a nexus of spiritual power or no.
Left to their own devices, the winged miscreants accrue loose baubles, hording them in filthy dens as often as not established in our cupboards and privies. Seemingly possessed of an antiquity dealer's discernment, each prefers to pilfer the most valuable paraphernalia and potent artifacts, yet they remain pathetically inept in the use of even the simplest gewgaw.
I admit the imp's general incompetence makes them appealing retainers. One of the little cretins may displace a favored wand of elemental power, but little peril exists of it activating the instrument and immolating your collected volumes of arcana.
The same cannot be said of apprentices.
Yet the beasts present a danger to the unwary, for they possess a low cunning not unlike that of xaurips and orlans. Without a domineering hand to direct them, imps rapidly regress to their base instincts. As a result of their propensity for pack behavior, even transitory leniency with a single imp can imperil a wizard's entire collection.
Acquisition
Arkemyr's Manor
: In Arkemyr's bedroom, in the bookcase on the wall.

On the Fire-Forged Path: The Travels of Gjaryc Yltan
General
Slot

Book

a2000aa2-3275-42db-813a-e9a6f40ff72d
On the Fire-Forged Path: The Travels of Gjaryc Yltan
is a
book
in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
. It is about a
Magranite
's pilgrimage to
Neketaka
, the
Waelites
of
Neketaka
, and the various worshippers in
The Sacred Stair
.
Description
Excerpt from
On the Fire-Forged Path: the Travels of Gjaryc Yltan
.
"Though I was born and raised a Magranite - and a Magranite, now, I will stay - as a young man I undertook a pilgrimage to visit a holy house dedicated to every god. In so doing, I hoped to know them each the better, to take what they had to teach and sow it into my soul like so many seeds, that my soul might grow and bear only the most delectable fruit for my goddess to devour at the moment of my death. So it is with no small amount of amusement that I pen this account of my visit once to a church of Wael, the many-eyed, many-tongued god of dreams and secrets, revelations and mysteries, and reveal to you all I learned there.
The challenge came first in finding adherents to Wael's doctrine, for they are not often ones to announce their presence, preferring instead to build their flock from the solitary seekers who delve through ancient ruins and ruined archives in search of the strange, the bizarre, the forgotten. But persistence is my goddess' first teaching, and find them I did.
The Waelites' Neketakan congregation was small then, as it likely remains now, and on the morning I stumbled upon them, they were lounging like so many cats in the sun on the steps above Queen's Berth, sharing between them a bottle of arrack and pipes packed with whiteleaf and ripple sponge. I knew them for Waelites not for any badge or robe or trinket they wore, not for their race or age, but for the ardor of their debate on the most benign of topics.
I begged that they take me to their church and permit me to worship with them, and they laughed as one, their many voices like the howling of wild dogs. They acquiesced when I told them of my quest, and then invited me to sit and share their drink. I did, and as the arrack burned a trail of fire down my throat, they showed me the dimensions of their hall of worship. The stairs were their pews, they said, the blue sky their ceiling, and their walls the edges of the world. All of creation sits within its bounds.
As morning neared midday, they stood as one and began to climb the mountain. 'Where do you go now?' I asked. 'To worship!' They replied. A great wave of relief washed over me, for at last I would have my lesson from them. We climbed the many steps of Neketaka and arrived at last in the Sacred Stair. 'Where is your temple?' I asked, and in response they whooped like children, rushing past me in a squall of smoke and laughter. I followed as best I could, though I wet my good slippers in a stream and could hardly keep my feet on the moss-slick stones, and we surged soggy-footed and hollering into the Temple of Gaun.
'To worship! To worship!' They cried. We shoved past Dawnstars bent in praise of their macabre god, laughing all the while, and came to stand before a leafless tree whose boughs were hung in lanterns too numerous too count. I had nary a moment to catch my breath before the Waelites were clambering into the great tree's branches. A young man pulled me up with one hand and handed me a pipe with the other. The priests of Gaun screeched and wailed, and all the while we squawked like birds, our smiles wide and eyes alight with arrack and lantern fire. The Mataru came soon after to chase us away, but not before we'd done our share of singing to the many-eyed, many-tongued god of dreams.
Would that I could have stayed with them a while longer, but alas, I could not deny my soul its journey nor the whispers of my goddess in my ear. I took again to the road in search of churches, but I must admit, I longed always after for that tree."
Acquisition

PAGE: On the Provenance and Ruination of Neketaka's 'Old City'
CATEGORIES: Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire lore items

On the Provenance and Ruination of Neketaka's 'Old City'
General
Slot
Unequippable
Item type
Document
Category
Other item
Sell value
16
Buy value
80
Technical
Item ID
Lore_Book_Old_City_Lecture
Guid
03e6163b-1b01-48ca-a02c-186801b807f9
On the Provenance and Ruination of Neketaka's 'Old City'
is a
document
in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
. It is about the
Old City
beneath
The Gullet
in
Neketaka
.
Description
Excerpt from a lecture given before the annual convention of the academy of architectural historians in Aedyr.
"Close examination by learned parties suggests that Neketaka is significantly older than it might at first appear.
We take as our example the suppurating wound in the city's side, which the locals most charmingly refer to as 'the Gullet.' On its face, it is not considerably different from your average slum. Indeed, it contains all that one might expect of such a place - desperate poverty, wrenching hunger, a tavern fair brimming with miscreants, and a flourishing criminal culture. Of course, it has its own unique offering, as well - a towering pile of garbage dumped into the district from the more affluent neighborhoods above it. It is, in every sense, abominable. The Huana leadership should be ashamed.
But I digress. Far more interesting than the caste stratifications among the Huana are the bones their city is built upon - for beneath 'the Gullet' lies a vast cavern littered with the remains of an ancient city. Referred to simply as the 'Old City' by the denizens of Neketaka, this sunken metropolis is notable for two reasons - the Old City's architecture is markedly different in style, form, and apparent use from the architecture of modern Neketaka, and there is no readily available explanation for the Old City's destruction that has not already been considered and discounted by those inclined to study it.
My peers here in the academy and beyond believe that the Old City's destruction is clearly the fault of the region's energetic volcanism and subsequent tectonic rumblings. I would caution against grasping at such easy solutions, however.
Consider the following -
The Huana have lived in the region for thousands of years. Earthquakes are no more a surprise to them than are the archipelago's daily soaking rains. None in Eora match their sheer creativity and expertise in building to withstand these events.
Moreover, for all their flexibility in building construction, the Huana's tastes have proven to be remarkably stable over time, showing a clear preference for designs that mimic the rhythm and shapes of the natural world. The Old City shows none of these things. Indeed, what remains was constructed primarily of stone cut in austere blocks, and the buildings are arranged in a manner not dissimilar from those prevalent in the Engwithan ruins that dot the landscape.
With those two points in mind, does it not seem prudent to ask whether the Old City is Huana in origin and, if it is not, who built it, and, finally, what destroyed it?"
Acquisition
Tikawara
,
Kuaru Hut
: In a hidden drawer on the left.

My peers here in the academy and beyond believe that the Old City's destruction is clearly the fault of the region's energetic volcanism and subsequent tectonic rumblings. I would caution against grasping at such easy solutions, however.
Consider the following -
The Huana have lived in the region for thousands of years. Earthquakes are no more a surprise to them than are the archipelago's daily soaking rains. None in Eora match their sheer creativity and expertise in building to withstand these events.
Moreover, for all their flexibility in building construction, the Huana's tastes have proven to be remarkably stable over time, showing a clear preference for designs that mimic the rhythm and shapes of the natural world. The Old City shows none of these things. Indeed, what remains was constructed primarily of stone cut in austere blocks, and the buildings are arranged in a manner not dissimilar from those prevalent in the Engwithan ruins that dot the landscape.
With those two points in mind, does it not seem prudent to ask whether the Old City is Huana in origin and, if it is not, who built it, and, finally, what destroyed it?"
Acquisition
This item's location is currently unknown.
Know where to find this item?
Contribute
to this page and share your knowledge!

On the Treatment and Preservation of Cannons
is a
document
in
The White March - Part II
.
Description
This page seems to be from some larger text.
"We now have a treatment to prevent our prized cannons from rusting outside. Potionmaster Andren developed a solution that seals the metal, protecting it from cold air. We've transformed the old armory into a 'patination chamber' where we can heat the solution into a gas. As the gas suffuses the chamber, it will build up a hard coating on the cannons. After a few weeks, the cannons will be ready for the elements.
However, we must be careful around the solution. One of Andren's assistants scalded her throat just from breathing too close to the stuff."
The rest of the manuscript has fallen apart over time.

Pelden's Note
is a
document
and
quest item
in
The White March - Part I
.
Description
"Pelden,
You're the most talented of my apprentices. But your understanding is merely a page among the tomes of knowledge I've accumulated.
Curb your pride until you've earned it. No weakness is deadlier.
I can almost see your hands shaking and your face reddening as you read this. You think that mastering a few basic hexes makes you my worthy pupil? I'd crafted the Parasitic Staff when I was half your age.
And while I worked, my peers plotted against me.
You may have surpassed the others for now, but they will band together against you if you give them reason. Conceal your skill with mistakes. Hide your malice behind smiles. Sacrifice your vanity for a few precious years that you might survive long enough to earn the title of 'wizard.'"
Acquisition
Crägholdt
: Dropped by
Pelden
.
Usage
Reading this item allows you to answer the question
"Which weakness is deadliest?"
asked by the door to Concelhaut's study in
Crägholdt
. The correct response is
"Pride."

and
quest item

Description
Most of the writing and illustrations on the scroll are illegible from a combination of age and water damage. One passage has survived entropy's touch:
Periki's Devotion
Pitied is Ngati, Lady of Lament.
As the pearl orb of the heavens crosses her view,
Her eyes well with tears as constant as rain.
But the moon's skyward journey continues apace,
The lovers' affection as ephemeral as fingers touching.
Acquisition
Cannot be obtained in-game without the use of console commands.
Notes
This item contains the passage used to open the entrance to the ruins where the sea dragon
Scyorielaphas
resides under the
Watershapers Guild
in
Periki's Overlook
. While it would have been used during the quest
The Shadow Under Neketaka
, the words are instead given to you by the spirit of
Guildmaster Mairu
.

Pillars of Eternity
Document
Game
Avowed
Journal
Lore
Region
Fort Northreach
Pillars of Eternity
is an examinable
document
in
Avowed
.
Document
Pillars of Eternity
Adra is a green crystal found throughout the known world, emerging from the crust of Eora in the shape of iconic pillars. We cherish adra. Build our temples around it. Study its potential as an energy source.
But adra is so much more! When we die, adra is the road on which our souls travel into the Beyond. And when our souls are ready to return, adra shines a lantern guiding us from death into life.
When you find yourself in the presence of adra, take a moment to ponder your place in the great Wheel. Consider who you were, who you are, and who you can be.
Acquisition
Fort Northreach

Poko Kohara Expedition Log
is a
journal
in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Description
This leather-bound logbook has "Property of the
Vailian Trading Company
" stamped inside its cover. Most of the pages are dark brown and stiff, stained with some dark, aromatic beverage.
A few pages have been ripped from the end.
"We set out at dawn on orders from
Governor Alvari
. She's heard rumor of luminous adra at a place called
Poko Kohara
. Unfortunately, the place is said to be surrounded by storms, and it doesn't appear on any of our charts, but we're told the locals at
Tikawara
may be able to help.
20 Préauton
I'd heard stories of bad run-ins with Huana tribes, but Chieftain
Ruānu
and the tribe at Tikawara welcomed us warmly. Fed us as well as could be expected and marked Poko Kohara on our maps. He seems to believe the storms are magical, or else the will of the gods. I hold out hope that they can be stopped.
2 Majauton
Left for Poko Kohara this morning.
Vektor
wasn't happy about being left behind, but he was too sick to travel and
Beza
was losing patience. Haven't seen a Rauataian ship since we left Neketaka, but she's still afraid they'll beat us there.
5 Majauton
Storms were some of the worst I've seen, but we made it. We set up camp by the cliffs, but we're all looking forward to getting into the ruins. At least it'll be dry in there.
7 Majauton
We lost
Gian
and
Olara
today. I don't know what, but something about this place seems off. The others feel it, too.
? Majauton
The murals here are incredible - proof that the Engwithans met ancient Huana two thousand years ago! That they might have even built this place! I keep trying to explain this to Beza, but she won't listen.
? Majauton
We found the top of the adra vein. It is glowing, but Beza says we have to go deeper."
Acquisition
Engwithan Waystation Level Two
: Found on the body of
Dueno
.
Trivia
Based on the dates, the expedition starts occurs approximately 18 days prior to the revival of the Watcher on
The Defiant
, and the start of the game.
The log is assumed to be written by
Falero
, one of the members of the expedition. It can be found on the body of Dueno - it assumed that he stole it from Falero.
Other member of the party include:
Vektor
, who was sick and decided not to continue to the ruins.
Beza
, leader of the expedition. You can talk to her soul on level four.
Gian
, he is killed by the Engwithan Titan outside.
Olara
, she is the first to enter the ruins after activating the titan. She is killed by a spike trap after being pushed by Dueno, on level one.
Dueno
, killed by Beza on level two, found by Beza and Falero with a sword in his back.
Falero
, is killed by an Engwithan Saint on level three.

======================================================================
PAGE: Precepts and Proverbs of Abydon
CATEGORIES: The White March - Part I lore items
URL: https://pillarsofeternity.fandom.com/wiki/Precepts_and_Proverbs_of_Abydon
======================================================================

Precepts and Proverbs of Abydon
[WM1]
General
Slot
Unequippable
Item type
Journal
Category
Other item
Sell value
0
Buy value
0
Technical
Item ID
misc_book_battery_precepts
Precepts and Proverbs of Abydon
is a
journal
in
The White March - Part I
about the
diety
Abydon
.
Description
"For every work there is a practice. Arm yourself with skill and temper your labors with patience.
Strike only when your medium is ready. Do not cold work plate.
Brittle steel is worse than a treacherous friend. Temper your work lest it shatter like glass.
Fools praise appearance, but the master praises strength.
True virtue lies in work well done. Pattern-welded steel shall be folded no fewer than seven times.
The finest smith cannot shape poor metals. Set your hand to steels that have been properly treated with charcoal.
Like a room full of discord is a forge with uneven heat. Do not let it pervert your metal.
As the blows of the hammer speak to the steel, so the color of the steel speaks to the smith.
Like a babe is heated steel, fragile and easily corrupted. Handle it gently, lest your haste twist and warp it.
Do not neglect work that lies hidden and unseen, for a shoddy tang can break the blade.
The wise smith works carefully and anneals but once. The careless smith weeps to find flaws after the steel has been hardened and tempered.
As a blade drawn in multiple heats is work done in its proper time."
Acquisition
[WM1]
Durgan's Battery (Foundry)
: Wooden box in the northernmost room across from the map room.

Ye exiles, ye broken, fear not the vengeance of the Burned Queen
She watches from her throne, ever vigilant.
She hears the oath thou doth speak at her altar.
She hears the oath thou doth speak in thine home.
She hears the oath thou doth speak in the dark.
For ye who would keep thy word, thou shalt escape the justice of her gaze.

Beware, for the eye of Woedica will not be blinded.
She hears the sundered oath.
She is not fooled by the winding path.
She attends the broken promise.
She sees the deceiver.
There is no shadow too dark. Her gaze will find thee. Her justice will not be restrained.
The fires of justice will never be quenched.
The throne will crack
The law will burn
But the queen that was always will be.
Speak not an untruth or thy tongue will be bound .
Remember thy place.
Remember thine oath.
Remember thy queen.

.
Description
If not for the food shortage, Ruānu would ask for what I bring so many crabs from the beach. They take to the sand at midnight and scuttle around my feet - as hungry as the rest of us, I say. The work is difficult enough without them pinching my ankles and going after the prize.
I thank Ngati for every day that Ruānu does not ask.
The shore warms by day and cools by night. If this will get the job done, then even Kohopa may forgive me. Only at midnight can I check. Some day the tribe will know what I do, but until that day... ekera, no one may know.
In the meantime, I say the beach is so lonely.
Acquisition
Tikawara
,
Kuaru Hut
: In a chest at the back of the area.

PAGE: Scrawled Letter (Valewood)
CATEGORIES: Pillars of Eternity lore items
URL: https://pillarsofeternity.fandom.com/wiki/Scrawled_Letter_(Valewood)
======================================================================

Scrawled Letter
General
Slot
Unequippable
Item type
Letter
Sell value
0
Buy value
2
Related
Items
Fulvano's Gloves
Page from Fulvano's Travels (gloves clue)
Technical
Item ID
misc_note_dead_traveller_vwd
Scrawled Letter
is a
letter
in
Pillars of Eternity
.
Description
"I do not think you will ever see this, but you were right, Fulvano. We should have journeyed south together, and been safer for it. I would tolerate all the gloating in the world if I might live to hear it. I have put myself out of reach of the beasts circling below, but I am done for all the same. I do not think I will rise again. Whoever finds this - pray for me. Perhaps in the next life I shall be a trapper of wolves."
Acquisition
Valewood
: Found on a dead body on top of the climbable ruin.
Trivia
This letter is the dying words of a man from
New Heomar
, who was travelling with
Fulvano
days earlier. As he wished to continue north to
Geiran's Grasp
, the pair split up at
Gilded Vale
, with Fulvano continuing south to
Anslög's Compass
. After being attacked by wolves in
Valewood
, the man managed to climb out of reach, but was fatally injured. This note describes his regret for not listening to Fulvano, where he might have been safer travelling with a companion.
Had the man continued with Fulvano, it's likely that both would still be alive today. In addition, it's likely that the Dyrwoodan woman who
guided
Fulvano from Gilded Vale would still be alive, as Fulvano wouldn't have had the need for a guide.

PAGE: Scroll of Wael
CATEGORIES: Pillars of Eternity lore items
URL: https://pillarsofeternity.fandom.com/wiki/Scroll_of_Wael
======================================================================

Scroll of Wael
General
Slot
Unequippable
Item type
Document
Category
Quest item
Sell value
0
Buy value
0
Related
Quests
The Parable of Wael
Technical
Item ID
quest_scroll_wael
Scroll of Wael
is a
document
and
quest item
in
Pillars of Eternity
.
Description
This ancient scroll is bound with silver thread. The broken wax seal is stamped with the shape of an eye.
The scroll at first appears to be gibberish, a collection of symbols and characters with no apparent connection between them. As you study them, however, you could swear that the characters begin to move. Slowly, almost imperceptibly, they shift and crisscross and realign, and you are able to read the text:
"A simpleton seeks out a wise man said to know the answer to every question.
'Please,' says the simpleton, 'You have to help me. The world terrifies me. I wake each morning, and I don't know why. I make choices each day, and I don't know what will happen as a result. I go to sleep each night, and I don't know whether it will be my last.'
When the simpleton finishes, he notices that the wise man is weeping. The simpleton apologizes profusely and asks the wise man what he has said to upset him.
The wise man shakes his head and wipes the tears from his eyes. He answers, 'Some people have all the luck.'"
Acquisition
Woodend Plains
: Dropped by
Iben
during
The Parable of Wael
.
Usage
Central to the quest
The Parable of Wael
. The archivist
Grimda
wants you to recover the scroll (doing so nets you
Footpad's Hood
and a
Key to the Elder Archive
), but
Wael
wants it to remain lost and asks you to bury it (doing so will open up
Wael
's ending for
Memories of the Ancients
).

Sealed Missive
General
Slot
Unequippable

The Sealed Missive
Items
Open Missive
Technical
Item ID
quest_item_sealed_missive
This article is about the quest item. For the related quest, see
The Sealed Missive
.
Sealed Missive
is a
letter
and
quest item
in
Pillars of Eternity
.
Description
The scroll case is crafted of darkly-stained oak in the likeness of a thin tower. Along its length, five wax seals adorn the case, each with its own symbol: a small flame, an open palm, a crescent moon, a shining sun and balanced scale.
Acquisition
Elmshore
: Given to you by a
Dying Monk
in the northeastern corner of the map. This starts the quest
The Sealed Missive
.
Usage
When player receives the missive, they may decide either to keep the missive unopened,
to break open the missive, or to open the missive and seal it again (with
Dexterity
18). This is the only opportunity to do so.
If the missive is broken open, the
Open Missive
is added to the stash:
The wax seals break easily under your fingers as you pry open the scroll case. You unroll the scroll, seeing an official watermark through the delicate parchment.
If the missive is carefully opened:
With a measured hand, you very slowly massage the wax seals until you feel each seal slowly give way without cracking. When you are done, each seal appears visibly intact, and only a small application of heat is needed to reseal the container and hide any evidence of tampering.
Before you do so, you read the scroll contained within...

PAGE: Selected Correspondences of Giftbringer Iden

Selected Correspondences of Giftbringer Iden
General

lore_book_god_ondra
Selected Correspondences of Giftbringer Iden
is a
book
in
Pillars of Eternity
, it is about the
deity
Ondra
.
Description
Sing, oh ocean waves, of Ondra's sorrow - of her unrequited love for the unattainable moon! Sing of the ocean's sorrow, so that we may forget our own! Each day, the tides reenact Ondra's longing for the great moon - the waters reach out at high tide, yearning for the heavenly body, only to slump into low tide when the moon proves unattainable.
You asked me once why I loved Ondra so dearly - how I could go from a life on dry land to being a devote to the Goddess of the Oceans. I sing of the ocean's sorrow so that I may forget my own. It is Ondra's message that speaks to my heart - I have devoted my life to helping others discard painful memories, for that is the gift Ondra gave me. When I lost my young daughter, my wife and I were inconsolable until a Giftbearer offered to take my toddler's toys and cast them into the deepest waters.
Truth be told, I and the other Giftbearers I know have never even spoken to Ondra... she is largely silent and when she does 'speak' she uses floods and tidal waves instead of words. But we sing of the ocean's sorrow so that others may forget theirs. Ondra's story - the story of desire unanswered - actually matters to people like you and me. Magran cannot steer you to victory over sadness, Hylea cannot force joy down a crying throat... only Ondra can give us the strength to persevere when life seems without worth. And that is the answer to your question regarding why I love my Goddess so dearly.
Acquisition
The Hall of Revealed Mysteries
,
Copperlane
: Bookcase facing southwest, last row on the right.

PAGE: Ship's Log of the Tempest Turn

Ship's Log of the
Tempest Turn
is a
book
in
Pillars of Eternity II: Deadfire
.
Description
An excerpt from the journal of Noran, former First Mate of the Tempest Turn. It reeks of stale liquor and whiteleaf smoke.
"Day 286
Suppose this is more of a diary now (though let's be honest, it was heading that course for some time now) on account of Captain Deluna kicking me from the ship. And all because I kept reminding her how she said one night over dinner she'd finally listen to my theories on that crew who went missing near some island - (what was it called, Bloodlung Island or Kazuwari or something such?) - to the north of Fort Deadlight. I don't remember. Point is, I know it wasn't the Floating Hangman what got them cause the dhow was recovered and it didn't have no blood on the deck nor even any torn sails or pockmarked wood. For that matter, it couldn't have been those trading company bastards, ship hunters, slavers, Huana savages, or aumaua military.
The crew just up and disappeared. Every last one. No bodies. No blood. Just clothes and food and grog left behind. Gods, THEY LEFT THE GROG! Every last cask.
So you tell me, Captain Deluna, just what happened to them? What new threat's out there what we ought to be spending gold and rubies and blood and sweat to prepare for?!
Who took them if it wasn't a flock of overly cunning imps with the taste for pirate flesh?
Well, I'm going to find out. Just as soon as I charter a ship to that island."
Acquisition

"Burn
Feel thy hatred twist within thee.
Feed thyself on its bile, sustain thyself on its anger.

Small Book
Document

Avowed

Lore

SmallBook
Examinable ID

EXAM_
SmallBook
Small Book
is an examinable
document
in
Avowed
.
Document
Small Book
The reduced size of this book indicates that it was made for the hands of kith smaller than you. Despite this, the book is still easy enough to read. An old, faded bookmark denotes a favored passage:
At the sound of heavy footfalls approaching and then moving past Cordhwn's hideaway, he couldn't help but smile affectionately. His lover had never been very observant, so it was no surprise that the dwarf had missed the hidden entrance despite Cordhwn's instructions. The young orlan, diminutive even among his own people, leaned forward and poked his head out between the curtains. His voice was an amused whisper as he called out.
"Vansar! Down here!"
Cordhwn stifled a laugh as Vansar jumped in surprise at the voice behind him. The dwarf's annoyance quickly faded to an amused acceptance as he saw the delight clear as day on his orlan paramour's face.
"Fuitu, Cordwhn! You nearly scared me straight to Berath's realm!"
Cordhwn rolled his eyes at the exaggeration and quickly darted back into his hideaway. Moments later, Vansar's grunts heralded his entrance into Cordhwn's small den. It was a cozy little place, tucked into the outer walls of the ciy, full of pillows and a single dim lantern turned down low. Cordhwn gave Vansar a small kiss on the cheek once the dwarf had finished squeezing his way into the den.
"I'm sorry about the shock, really," Cordhwn said. "But seeing you jump like that was pretty funny. Anyway, what do you think? Not a bad place to hide, huh?"
Vansar looked around thoughtfully. He couldn't help but begrudgingly admit that it was a cozy little place to pass an evening. Not that he'd say as much to Cordhwn, of course. Instead, he simply shrugged.
"Oh, don't be such a stick in the mud, Vansar," Cordhwn teased. "Guess I'll just have to prove how nice of a hideout it is, huh?"
Without waiting for a response, Cordhwn dove at Vansar, catching him by surprise and tackling him to the ground. As their lips met and orlan fur entwined with dwarven beard, the pair felt truly home.

“Admeth set the forest aflame, they say. Admeth snatched the sharpest fang out of the enemy’s jaws, they sing.
I know nothing beyond the walls of my cell, but I still have my memories - and I don’t recall a single crisped tree on that battlefield. I don’t recall being taken. I remember waving the flag of parley and having it answered with a battlecry. Anything they burned they burned later.
History isn’t written by the victors or kith who were there. It’s written by scribes, and for some reason Admeth isn’t of a mind to contradict their lies. Maybe it’s because he’s where he is, and I’m where I am. There’s history and there’s ‘history.’ Takes a keen eye to tell the difference.
~ Regd.”
