Document
Writings of Soreena IV
Why are we like this? Why do we hurl ourselves across the world to scatter our bones on far and fallow shores?
There are two stories about the long lives of dwarves.
One story says that the gods made us strong so that we could challenge the world and endure. We live long lives because we are so well made.
But when I look upon these Living Lands, I wonder. There are no aged beasts here. There are no old behemoths in such a fecund place. The change, the ferment – it kills the old, buries it, composts it into a feast for the new. Even the stone is young!
Would the gods really make us strong and stolid and stubborn? If they meant us to voyage across strange and everchanging seas, and to change to suit the lands we found? Each spring I see the ants and the bees send out their mating flights, and I wonder. Why aren’t we that way? Quick and fecund?
I favor the other story.
Dwarves are long-lived because once, long ago, we dwelled in stasis. Our ways were fixed as stone. Only old age could kill us, so we grew very good at aging.
Then something changed. Some flaw came into us, some cataclysm overturned our cozy cup of a home. Some sin or fear tainted us. Perhaps the slow cycle of our souls through the same long, narrow lives became intolerable. And so we went out into the world like sparks from the forge, to set our little fires wherever we landed.
So often those fires go out. Not because we are weak or frail, but because we are so stiff and strong and slow to change.
Why are we cursed to wanderlust, when we are so unsuited to it?
Perhaps that is what it means to be a dwarf. To engineer what is unsuited into what is required. To refashion ourselves into newer better shapes, no matter how painful the change.
But if this is so—
Why did Nandru turn back from his destiny?
Why are his secret books torn between the call of his dreams and fear of his fate?
What change was too painful for him to face? Why did he stop and settle Solace, instead of following the call to its source?
I have chosen a new way for Solace, and shut Nandru’s secrets away forever. But I wonder…
Do dwarves wander the world because we are fleeing the stasis of a settled home? Or because we are searching for something we have yet to find?
Acquisition

Document
Writings of Soreena V
In hope for the renewal of Solace, the scholar Soreena, who is called the Strict, presents these flakes to the families of the Keep, that they might by debate and dissemination be knapped into sharp points:
I. When our founder Nandru said “Do not alter what I have taught you,” he intended that we live our entire lives in accordance with his teachings.
II. The people of Solace have turned away from Nandru’s Word because the stone where that Word was carved has been lost.
III. But the Word was never in the Stone. The Word was in the people. It is the responsibility of the people to rebuild the broken Word.
IV. The Word of Nandru instructs us to build a mighty fortress and to marshal our power within it, that it should stand even when the world’s foundations quiver.
V. Therefore it is the responsibility of the people to rebuild the might of this fortress even as we rebuild the Word.
VI. Obedience to the Word of Nandru is false unless it is accompanied by investment in the world of Nandru, that is, labor in the service of Solace. To divest from Solace is to disobey Nandru.
VII. There should be no wealthy in Solace until Solace is wealthy again. The paid exemption to corvee should end unless the payment goes to fund the corvee.
VIII. There should be no safe in Solace until Solace is safe again. The paid exemption from service in the Wardens should end unless the payment goes to fund the Wardens.
IX. Neither station of birth nor status of the quarter should except anyone from labor in service of Solace.
X. There should be no Word of Nandru except the word that is practiced. There should be no written Word that overrules the Word that is spoken.
XI. The body of law that has been recorded since the day of Nandru, in the interpretation of Nandru’s life and teachings, which is to say the Lessons of Nandru, has no legitimacy and should be closed unread.
XII. The strength of Solace is in Solace. Citizenship cannot be purchased, but only earned through works.
XIII. It is said among some kith that tradition for tradition’s sake stifles change. Indeed steel must bend lest it shatter. But does the ship keep its keel only for keel’s sake? Yea, the keel stifles change, so that the ship will not overturn. Does the foundation keep its cornerstones only for corners’ sake? Yea, the cornerstone stifles change, so that the wall will not topple.
XIV. In all things Nandru’s Word prefers the tested way to the untested. We are all sorely tested, and we must return to the tested way.
XV. The Word of Nandru should not be reserved for the literate. All should have equal access to the Word.
XVI. The right to serve upon the Council should not be conditioned upon knowledge of the written Lessons, but only upon knowledge of Nandru’s Word as it was spoken.
XVII. The first use of the smithy should be to arm and armor Solace. The last use should be ingots for trade.
XVIII. Any smith who is held in debt bondage to a trading family, and who practices Abydon’s craft to pay down that debt, should be released; that debt should be annulled.
XIX. The penalty for placing oneself before Solace should be service. Those who believe they can be exempted from the work of defending and building Solace because of their wealth or heritage should be the first slain in battle and set the deepest in the mines.
XX. But for those of wealth and heritage who place Solace before themselves there should be recognition, and reward, as there is recognition for the keystone and the lintel and the column; they are the columns of Solace, they are the keystones and the lintels.
XXI. Those who interpret the Word of Nandru from the Lessons of Nandru and the custom of the law are the enemies of Solace. Those who seek the Word of Nandru in the spoken teachings of Nandru are the heart and the hand of Solace.
Acquisition

The looping scribbles are difficult to read, but as you flip through the pages, you can make out several passages. Near the beginning, you read:
"...will be a suitable place for my experiments. There's an abundance of space, and, more importantly, the locals are content to ignore it. I could probably constr..."
You skip ahead several pages.
"...willing volunteers. The Legacy has brought many grievances to the surface, and capturing the essence is primarily a matter of timing. The ritual of the Effigy serves as a good template for..."
You scan the middle of the book.

You turn to the last page.
"...noble from Defiance Bay. Results were mostly consistent across the other subjects. The challenge is always applying the method to an unwilling participant, but her situation may prove an advantage. If I can bring those memories of her uncle to the forefront, it might render her essence more susceptible to the process."
